Free Talk

The Dr. Shang Zhongyi That I Know

— Zhuang Zexuan

Southern Guangdong is unfortunate, suffering cruel trampling. Educators who have left us have already been three in succession. Among the three, the death of Dr. Shang Zhongyi is the most sudden. However, among the three, my relationship with Shang is the deepest. Twenty years ago, when I went abroad, Shang was still studying at the Tsinghua Secondary Vocational School, and I did not know him. Fifteen years ago, when I returned to China to teach at Tsinghua, Shang was about to graduate. At that time, I also served as a career guidance officer. I knew that he was enthusiastic about social service and strongly urged him to study education. Shang also wanted to enter Peabody College for Teachers at Vanderbilt University. Peabody is a well-known normal college located in the southern United States, as famous as Columbia and Chicago. Previously, no Chinese students had gone there. After Shang entered, he received a warm welcome from the local people and teachers and students in the school. Later, Shang went to Columbia Teachers College and obtained a doctorate.

Six years ago, I went to Hangzhou to teach at Zhejiang University, while Shang was at the Zhejiang Changmiao People's Education Experimental School, training many teachers for the people. I met Mr. Meng Lin in Guling and learned that Peking University needed educational talents, so I sought Shang's consent. At that time, Shang had married Ms. Wang Lifang, a Tsinghua classmate and sister of Guijun, who specialized in music in the United States. The husband followed the wife in singing, which was extremely happy.

A year ago, when I fled to Guangdong due to the war, Shang was the acting director of the Education Research Institute of Zhongshan University, striving to promote wartime education. Before long, Mr. Zaiyang returned from overseas investigation. Brothers Zhu Youguang and Zeng Zhaosen hosted several banquets for Mr. Zaiyang at the Lingnan Reception Room, and Shang and I were both present. I remember that there was a tense debate on a certain issue. Later, General Wo Qi heard of Shang's name and invited him to join the Political Department. Shang worked diligently day and night, and was uncompromising in the face of danger. When Guangzhou was evacuated, Shang sent his family to Guilin so that he could concentrate on his work. Initially, I did not expect that Guangzhou would fall and Guilin would be bombed. Shang went north with the army, while Madam Shang and her children came to Hong Kong via an indirect route.

This time, Shang was planning to take a car from Shao through Shantou to Hong Kong, but the car encountered an unexpected disaster near Shunning. Everyone else was slightly injured, but Shang died in the line of duty. Alas, why does Heaven rob us of educators more than those in other professions? Shang was in the prime of his life. With more time, his contributions to education would not have been limited to what he had already accomplished. We are already familiar with Shang's contributions to wartime education. If his leadership is desired for postwar educational facilities but cannot be obtained, wouldn't that be a great loss to the future of the country and the nation!

Encounter

— Sun Zhenshi

After a round of poisonous interrogation, he was taken by several burly men into this dark iron prison. It was so narrow and suffocating, crowded with a large group of people. As soon as he entered, he almost tripped over a foot that was sticking out. Feeling his way forward, he sat down in the gap between people. He felt his brain expanding desperately, and every pore on his skin was exploding. A burst of soreness, a burst of numbness, he clenched his teeth subconsciously; his eyes gradually blurred and darkened, the world seemed to be spinning, and finally, he fainted.

A burst of intense pain woke him up again. Looking around, it was still pitch black. Some voices were groaning softly. A vague shadow flashed through his mind, and he silently sank into his memories.

One noon, he was about to walk out of the office when Captain Wang Zhongwen rushed over and whispered to him:

"Jin Gang, there is another task for you now. If you succeed, we will be even stronger."

"What is it?" He looked at Captain Wang.

Captain Wang immediately put his mouth close to his ear:

"Although we now have hundreds of comrades, we only have thirty or forty firearms. Under the paving in front of the ×× Elementary School gate in Town C, there are more than fifty short guns buried. They were left behind when the army retreated before. Now we are sending you to find a way to transport them out. As for how to transport them, you will have to see how things go when you get there." Captain Wang raised his head, looked at the blue sky, and continued quickly: "You must go tonight, it's good that you are familiar with the situation in the town."

So, in the twilight, he arrived in Town C and lodged in the home of an acquaintance. He began his activities.

Two weeks later, he led a group of enthusiastic young porters and sneaked into the uninhabited school at night, starting a difficult job. The river water beside the paving was flashing with black light in the dark night. A fishing boat was quietly waiting, urging them to work harder.

Using the light of the moon and stars, they dug and dug in the dark night. The soil was dug up several feet high, and a wide wooden board was discovered. It was said that under this, a pile of dark guns were buried. Countless eyes began to reveal waves of joy and happiness, and they used all their strength to tie the guns together and move them to the fishing boat parked by the river. The partners waiting on the fishing boat loaded the guns onto the boat and covered them with cloth.

The fishing boat began to move in the river, reflecting in the light of the stars and moon. The outline of the town was dreaming in a sweet sleep.

The surroundings were silent, and a sound of oars came from across the river. Before long, several strong beams of light shone on the boat, and a violent voice shouted: "What are you doing? Don't move!" Before the partners could put up a fight, the other side jumped over to the boat. So Jin Gang and his partners were taken to the pseudo-police station in a series. Before the interrogation, they were beaten severely by the yellow-clothed men stationed in the pseudo-police station. Fresh red blood burst out of their red skin, turning into a brownish-purple narrow brand on their bodies. After the beating, they were taken one by one to the interrogation room. Several hideous yellow-clothed men and puppet officials were sitting high above, revealing contemptuous sneers.

"Aren't you going to confess?" The voice from above floated in the air. Jin Gang was still standing calmly and solemnly, silently pondering. After a while, the side door of the interrogation room was lightly pushed open, and a young man in plain clothes came out casually, and saw Jin Gang, pretending to be surprised!

"Oh, it's Brother Jin Gang! What crime have you committed?"

He looked up and standing in front of him was Yang Yimin, a former classmate.

"Brother Jin Gang, joined the guerrillas? Haha - what a boring thing -"

Countless sparks burst out in Jin Gang's eyes. Before Yang Yimin finished speaking, he rushed towards him in one breath, and Yang Yimin was caught off guard and somersaulted.

After that, Jin Gang was dragged down and beaten severely by several burly men, fainting and waking up, waking up and fainting again, fainting and waking up several times. His whole body was red and swollen. In this way, he was pushed into this iron prison.

He missed the young porters and boatmen, and also missed his many comrades. In this way, he endured in prison, suffering hardships, waiting for an opportunity to break through the wall and fly away.

Dawn

— Ma Yufeng

Farmers are used to getting up early,

The sky is only slightly bright,

Someone is walking on the porch,

Followed by the sound of opening the door.

Mother starts a fire in the kitchen

And tells her younger sister,

To carry buckets to inspect the round fields,

The outdoors is hazy.

Prisoner

— Shen Si

The waning moon hangs on the government, accompanying us all the way. When the sun rises, we have already traveled twenty miles.

The roadside is full of places passed by the × army. In the villages on the west bank of the Fen River, there is not a single person's shadow.

We can no longer see the smoke rising from the chimneys in the morning, and we feel a continuous desolation in our hearts.

Dogs wandered on the roadside, licking the blood on the ground. In the distance, we saw the highway winding down from the mountain. Our alert troops were all over our heads.

Clap! Clap! Clap! It rang continuously.

As we passed the highway, four enemies fixed on this side of the highway from the village next to the highway.

We greeted them, and the quick gun rang loudly, and a Japanese soldier fell down.

"Surrender your guns, don't kill, treat you well!" The propagandist shouted slogans in Japanese, and our ranks continued to move forward

The other three Japanese soldiers ran to the village in front. Our soldiers, who were chasing closely behind, also shouted in Japanese.

We are the Eighth Route Army, we treat prisoners well.

Three living Japanese soldiers were disarmed.

I asked them: "Why are you deceived by the fascist warlords and come to China to be cannon fodder?"

They lowered their heads for a long time and did not speak.

Suddenly one of them spoke, his voice a little excited.

"We are fighting for the peace of East Asia, not for aggression."

I asked again:

"Fighting for peace, why come to China to forcibly occupy Chinese land, kill Chinese people, rape Chinese women, ...

He said, "Because China cannot understand."

I was a little angry and asked:

"What do you want us to understand?"

"I don't know what the government of my country thinks."

The political officer told them our proposition. He said, "We do not hate the Japanese people, we only want to overthrow the Japanese fascist warlords; most Japanese people are suffering just like us. We - Chinese and Japanese, should unite to attack the fascist bandits and relieve our own suffering.

They expressed their approval of the political officer's talk

The political officer's attitude was so sincere and sincere that it could really move people

Later, he said to them again: "If you come to China, you will never be able to go back, and your parents and wives at home will be thinking of you every day: If you come to China, you will not benefit!"

"Even if my family thinks of me, they will want to die!"

Tears came from the eyes of the three foreigners.

A cannon shot from Nanguan was very violent; so our political officer led a battalion of people to the mountains on both sides of the highway between Guangjiugu and Taohuapo. Prepare to intercept the passing motorcade.

The Solitary Walk

— Grass on the Wall

I have always enjoyed walking. When I say enjoy, it's not because I agree with hygiene enthusiasts that it's a beneficial physical and mental exercise. Actually, it's because I have too much free time; when I'm happy, I just wander around, and slowly it becomes a habit. When people develop a habit, they often do it unconsciously and automatically. For me, walking is a good example.

Most of my walks take place late at night, because during the day, there are too many vehicles on the street, and the crowds are relatively dense. As vehicles pass, they stir up dust, which goes straight into my nose, making it difficult to breathe. At night—or even at dusk—the soldiers and police are fewer, and the crowds are sparse. This allows me to walk freely without bumping into someone's shoulder, or having someone step on my shoes, which would make my leisurely mood anxious and violate the original purpose of walking.

I don't like walking with a large group of people, because the pleasure it offers is no longer based on walking. Even on a small scale, the different paces of each person can create a lot of trouble in the mind. However, I do enjoy walking with two people, as long as the other person truly understands the pleasure of walking. But, in reality, I am often alone, just me by myself.

Therefore, I laugh at myself as a solitary walker.

Because I have walked so much, I am familiar with so many streets suitable for walking, most of which are relatively quiet but not deserted. I walk slowly on them, always muttering something like a masterpiece of a poem. In fact, I often don't think about anything. I pay no attention to the things around me; or I feel something, I perceive something. I think I belong to another world, and at the same time, I think that world belongs exclusively to me. But when I realize that my body is actually in the human world, in the ordinary hustle and bustle, I have overlooked things? I calmly want to emphasize my observation to discover the fun in them. I will stop under dazzling neon lights, moving my gaze and silently enjoying the colors and structural beauty of various goods. I will follow behind graceful women to satisfy my sensory comfort. Yes, I also feel such loneliness, so I often urgently want to meet an acquaintance. Even if it's someone I've only met briefly, I'll greet them, cast a joyful glance, and of course, I need a sincere handshake and a heart-to-heart conversation, which will warm my soul.

But the streets are like the ocean, and in the vast ocean, I am unfamiliar with the crowds.

The night is deep, and people have already gone to sleep. On this street, there is only me.

I look at the stars in the sky. I think with a sense of gain and loss, like a philosopher trying to understand the secrets of the universe.

Friend, do you want to ask me what I'm thinking about?

I tell you, I miss the suburbs. How wonderful it would be to take a solitary walk in the suburbs. I want to go to the suburbs.

Snow on the Ground

— Shu Qun

As soon as the maid saw him, she immediately closed her mouth and shivered: she was like a lit candle, gradually melting away. She didn't dare to speak, only giving the detective some hints, as if to say:

"That guy, he's the bandit!"

So, the detective immediately pulled out his gun and watched Yu Wen. At this time, the maid slowly hugged Zhu Lin and dared to speak:

"Can't you see it's him?"

Zhu Lin was smart. She said:

"Are you crazy? Didn't he just come with me? Didn't you see him?"

"I saw him! But I just recognized him now! Miss, I remember his eyes, don't you think they're strange?"

"Don't talk nonsense!"

"Miss, who is he?"

"He's my friend!"

The detective's gun was quietly put away again. The maid was bored and lowered her head. In order to avoid the detective's and the maid's suspicion, Zhu Lin deliberately took Yu Wen's arm to show that this person was not to be violated because:

"He's my lover!" However, from the time they met until now, she didn't love him, just as he didn't love her. What he and she loved was the same third party—the country.

The snow has been falling for three days. This heavy snow is common, because it is the snow of Manchuria.

After this parting, she returned to her family and soon moved to a new address; he was soon transferred to another job and went to another place. Because of the changes on both sides, it was impossible to find out their addresses. For five years, all news was cut off. However, in these five years, they often asked their comrades, their friends:

"Do you know Zhu Lin?" and "Do you know Yu Wen?" (The End)
